        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462983419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6996299647960167661">This was probably the best Anita book I've since the...well since the ardeur (sp) started and Anita became a whore. Sorry to say that because I love Anita, but she did turn into quite the whore... it was getting to the point where I thought Ms. Hamilton had crossed wires, between the Anita Blake series and the Meredith Gentry series. Because in Anita's first 8 or 9 book maybe less she was this complete barney bad-ass that kicked anyone's ass the f****ed with her. Then she started turning into th</span>
  <span id="freeText6996299647960167661" style="display:none">This was probably the best Anita book I've since the...well since the ardeur (sp) started and Anita became a whore. Sorry to say that because I love Anita, but she did turn into quite the whore... it was getting to the point where I thought Ms. Hamilton had crossed wires, between the Anita Blake series and the Meredith Gentry series. Because in Anita's first 8 or 9 book maybe less she was this complete barney bad-ass that kicked anyone's ass the f****ed with her. Then she started turning into this whiny wimpering, sex fiend. Then in the Meredith books, she's supposed to sleep around with as many guys as possible, and that was the whole basis of the books, to stay alive, and screw as many fairies as possible to concieve a child to gain the throne. But somehow they both totally flip-flopped, Anita went into whore mode, and Merry turned into the barney bad ass. Now don't get me wrong I love both series, and I a still hoping the the Meredith Gentry series will continue for a little longer. It just seems odd how the main female character flip flops into what another lead female character in another story is supposed to be.<br /><br />Anywho, this book I enjoy immensely. One the lack of sex was great, it was a nice change of pace from how the series is going. Two you get to see Edward again, I just love him. Three Anita is having doubts about Nathaniel, well in my opinion... ABOUT DAMNED TIME. I like Nathaniel, but I don't see him as Anita's type, he's too submissive for my taste. Four the best best BEST part of the book, is when Anita went off on Richard, that she had finally had enough of his bullsh*t. Jean-Claude too it was so great, I was whooping for them both while reading that. Richard is a self rightous bastard, who doesn't know his a$$ from his head. I totally loved it though, never liked the guy... there was a book or two where I had thought that maybe he was deemable then he went and screwed things up again. Wish him the best but BUBYE BUCKAROO!</span>

<div id="review_92357374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Holly Full Moon Bites Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3238772-holly-full-moon-bites-book-reviews"><img alt="Holly Full Moon Bites Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493258056p2/3238772.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92357374?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly Full Moon Bites Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly Full Moon Bites Book Reviews" href="/user/show/3238772-holly-full-moon-bites-book-reviews">Holly Full Moon Bites Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3238772-holly-full-moon-bites-book-reviews?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92357374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3428625058182274517"><b>~Has slight spoilers.~</b><br/><br/>Anita Blake is calling in the big gun's-- Edward as The Harlequin, very old vampires who kill for the council and wear masks-- come to St. Louis. But Edward isn't the only one she is going to need--Jean-Claude and Richard must come together with Anita and her other trivium if they are to defend themselves against The Harlequin.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this fifteenth Anita Blake book. I think we get some of the good-action-suspense-plot back we had from the earlier Anita Blake books</span>
  <span id="freeText3428625058182274517" style="display:none"><b>~Has slight spoilers.~</b><br /><br />Anita Blake is calling in the big gun's-- Edward as The Harlequin, very old vampires who kill for the council and wear masks-- come to St. Louis. But Edward isn't the only one she is going to need--Jean-Claude and Richard must come together with Anita and her other trivium if they are to defend themselves against The Harlequin.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this fifteenth Anita Blake book. I think we get some of the good-action-suspense-plot back we had from the earlier Anita Blake books but we also still get the great sexual side that the series has come to include in the last few books.<br /><br />One thing that bothered me and I think I have mentioned before in another review is that I miss Dolph not this new Dolph, I miss the old Dolph! How he and Anita used to be, I know he is upset but the old Dolph I just don't think he would be acting this was--it seems out of character to me. The Dolph I knew wouldn't let his feelings or hate get in the way of police business.<br /><br />Haven is also back which I think deserves mentioning and I hope staying for good. Thug or not I liked him from the very beginning and hoped she would keep him.<br /><br />Altogether, I think this book is a step in the right direction of balancing the old Anita and the new Anita, so to speak.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to, again, people who liked the last couple of Anita Blake novels.</span>

<div id="review_119784692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119784692" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119784692?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119784692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7620120577194856830">Fifteenth in the Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter erotic urban fantasy series set in an alternate St. Louis, Missouri. The story revolves around Anita Blake's increasingly vampiric powers and the issues it creates for her and the people with whom she's involved.<br/><br/><b>The Story</b><br/>The Harlequin have come to St. Louis. A secret police force of vampire assassins who should abide by the rules when they come to town. Should being the operative word. But then the Vampire Council does fear Jean-Claude and his triumvi</span>
  <span id="freeText7620120577194856830" style="display:none">Fifteenth in the Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter erotic urban fantasy series set in an alternate St. Louis, Missouri. The story revolves around Anita Blake's increasingly vampiric powers and the issues it creates for her and the people with whom she's involved.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />The Harlequin have come to St. Louis. A secret police force of vampire assassins who should abide by the rules when they come to town. Should being the operative word. But then the Vampire Council does fear Jean-Claude and his triumvirate. So it's not that much of a surprise when all hell breaks loose and death comes shooting.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br />Richard is such an ass, blowing hot one minute and cold all the rest. Nathaniel is certainly feeling powerful these days while we learn a great deal about how Jean-Claude's guards feel about Anita and the <em>ardeur</em>. Malcolm certainly receives and returns the surprise of Anita's power. The lion pride in St. Louis gets a nasty shock and they certainly deserve it! Poor Raphael also gets a shock. It'll be interesting to see how he deals with the consequences of Anita's power in <em>Blood Noir</em>!<br /><br />Edward comes to help bringing a very unwanted pair of backups. And both Anita and Edward realize that their concept of fun has changed.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />Oh, wow! The action just never stops and the emotional tangles are just as intense BUT Anita is forced to see just how difficult she makes life for the men in her bed. She's an odd duck, our Anita. She hates being in love. Has no clue about relationships. Demands honesty and hates it when she gets it as she continually gets in her own way.<br /><br />I had doubted myself in the last story. Now it's confirmed. Jean-Claude and Anita have reinforced their "natural practicality" and she still doesn't know what J-C got from Richard. Hmmm, for as much in love with Anita as J-C is, I wonder if J-C got that desire for love from "our wolf"…<br /><br />Shockingly, Anita is learning not to poke. At least, not all the time.<br /><br />Thank god for the "police", I think. Who'da thunk vampires would have an enforcement group... Although, it's not surprising that there's rebellion within the ranks. The tension continues and the advancements tear on.<br /> <br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The cover is a bit scary with its scantily-clad Columbine casually leaning back against the warm brown and gold stone wall dangling an elaborate black-gold face mask from her fingertips, black ribbon crisscrossing her left forearm…a very feminine gauntlet.<br /><br />The title is much too apt as it is <em>The Harlequin</em> and their founder who are threatening everyone that Anita holds dear.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7620120577194856830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2144546?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/43779-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2144546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15627063422669434931">Series: #14 Anita Blake<br/><br/>Pages: 422<br/><br/>Number: 37<br/><br/>First Sentence:<br/><br/>"Malcolm the head of the Church of Eternal Life, the vampire church, sat across from me"<br/><br/>Synopsis:<br/><br/>From the Publisher<br/>Readers haven't seen anything yet-new in the "fabulously imagined series" (Publishers Weekly) from the #1 New York Times bestselling author.<br/><br/>Anita Blake is about to face the challenge of her life. Into her world-a world already overflowing with power-have come creatures so feared that powerful, centuries-old vampires refuse to</span>
  <span id="freeText15627063422669434931" style="display:none">Series: #14 Anita Blake<br /><br />Pages: 422<br /><br />Number: 37<br /><br />First Sentence:<br /><br />"Malcolm the head of the Church of Eternal Life, the vampire church, sat across from me"<br /><br />Synopsis:<br /><br />From the Publisher<br />Readers haven't seen anything yet-new in the "fabulously imagined series" (Publishers Weekly) from the #1 New York Times bestselling author.<br /><br />Anita Blake is about to face the challenge of her life. Into her world-a world already overflowing with power-have come creatures so feared that powerful, centuries-old vampires refuse to mention their names. It is forbidden to speak of The Harlequin unless you've been contacted. And to be contacted by The Harlequin is to be under sentence of death.<br /><br />Long-time rivals for Anita's affections, Jean-Claude, Master Vampire of the City, and Richard, alpha-werewolf, will need to become allies. Shapeshifters Nathaniel and Micah will have to step up their support. And then there's Edward. In this situation, Anita knows that she needs to call the one man who has always been there for her...<br /><br />My Thoughts:<br /><br />This series has always been one of my favorites. It is such a hotbed of animosity and discussion.<br />This is a series you either love, hate, or love to hate. There really is no inbetween. I am in love with this series period. I never thought that I would be a fan of anything vampire, after all they are the things horror movies are made of. But LKH was the author who made me fall in love with these types of stories.<br /><br />So far, we are seeing a totally different Anita. One who is in more control, one who is capable of staying in control even at moments when she used to snap.<br /><br />This journey into the Anitaverse brings a bit of the old Anita into the new Anita world and it was an extra spicy blend to an already hot world. Fans of the old Anita will see a glimpse of her in THE HARLEQUIN while fans of the new twist will not be let down either. It appears that LKH is starting to find her stride. And I believe it is clear in her dedication.<br /><br />Characterization:<br /><br />I truly feel like this is one of the best character driven series in this genre. LKH has created some of the most emotionally moving characters on paper. I fell in love with Nathaniel when he first appeared on paper, but I have to admit that as LKH has been allowing him to grow he really is one of my favorite literary heroes. I don't have many in fact my list is quite short.<br /><br />Keep/Swap/Library: Keep<br /><br />Rating: A</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10853648159360350653">The Harlequin is Anita Blake’s 15th book in the: Vampire Hunter series of PNR action and erotica novels by LKH.<br/><br/>The story starts with Malcolm in Anita’s office, telling she will be getting a warrant for the execution of some of his following in The Church of Eternal Life in St. Louis.   <span id="freeText10853648159360350653" style="display:none">The Harlequin is Anita Blake’s 15th book in the: Vampire Hunter series of PNR action and erotica novels by LKH.<br /><br />The story starts with Malcolm in Anita’s office, telling she will be getting a warrant for the execution of some of his following in The Church of Eternal Life in St. Louis. He has not required blood oaths of the vampires under him, hence he has no ability to keep them from becoming dangerous predators.<br /><br />Anita is known to be homophobic, and we find with long arguments with Nathaniel and Byron she is also not into BDSM as they are. She will get lessons from Asher sometime in the future.<br /><br />On a date with Nathaniel, Anita finds a gift box in the bathroom after a movie with her name on it from a group of vampires belonging to Marmée Noire (Mother of Darkness) called The Harlequin. In the box was a mask signifying that Harlequin were watching as potential adversaries.<br /><br />I used to be a Richard fan, but I have given up. So insecure and immature. I doubt if he’ll ever get over not being human. Gah! Being large is good, big ego is bad, being STUPID is unacceptable. Anita is always angry with him. Flush him!<br /><br />The overwhelming amount of sex from the Danse Macabre was not echoed in this story, and delightfully, there actually was more story to digest. I wish I would have read this on my Kindle to do a word count on <i>
  <b> I’m sorry. </b>
</i> EGAD!<br /><br />I enjoyed this story with less arduer and more action. Olaf was sure eerie. I’m off to get Blood Noir. <br /></span>

<div id="review_12921322" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12921322" />

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10159248688250676325">I am getting so tired of Richard the werewolf and his angst. Hopefully, Hamilton is too. Anyway, this time, the vampire police have come to town. They're messing with Malcolm and his non-blood-oathed religious vampires—or somebody is—and they don't seem to be following the vampire cop rules. So she calls Edward for help—and he brings his stepson. There's lots of blood and mayhem. Lots of angst from Richard. Lots of sex. And there may be the final straw with Richard. I liked it anyway. A lot.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2377092378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377092378" />
    <a title="Autumn Miller ~ autumnbookreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66604997-autumn-miller-autumnbookreads"><img alt="Autumn Miller ~ autumnbookreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528222708p2/66604997.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Autumn Miller ~ autumnbookreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Autumn Miller ~ autumnbookreads" href="/user/show/66604997-autumn-miller-autumnbookreads">Autumn Miller ~ autumnbookreads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66604997-autumn-miller-autumnbookreads?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377092378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18332815573408866590"><b> 4.5 Stars </b><br/>This installment in the Anita Blake was surprisingly good. In my review of the last book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/121927.Danse_Macabre__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___14_' title='Danse Macabre (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #14) by Laurell K. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Danse Macabre</a>, I said that this series had lost my interest and I was feeling like this series had run its course. I questioned how <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9550.Laurell_K__Hamilton' title='Laurell K. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laurell K. Hamilton</a> could continue with the same story lines over and over again. I felt like the series was getting repetitive and a <b>big</b> part of me wanted to stop reading it all together.<br/>I am so glad that I took a step back and waited a few months before coming back</span>
  <span id="freeText18332815573408866590" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 Stars </b><br />This installment in the Anita Blake was surprisingly good. In my review of the last book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/121927.Danse_Macabre__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___14_" title="Danse Macabre (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #14) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Danse Macabre</a>, I said that this series had lost my interest and I was feeling like this series had run its course. I questioned how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9550.Laurell_K__Hamilton" title="Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Laurell K. Hamilton</a> could continue with the same story lines over and over again. I felt like the series was getting repetitive and a <b>big</b> part of me wanted to stop reading it all together.<br />I am so glad that I took a step back and waited a few months before coming back to this series. I don't know if it is because of the time distance between reads or if this installment was just that good, but my love for the Anita Blake series has been renewed. This installment gave me everything that I had been lacking in the previous book and it has made me want to come back to this series again. <br />Yes, there are still parts of this series that really annoy me (Richard in particular), but for the most part, I had a lot of fun while reading this book and the good outweighs the bad for me. This series will never be on my top favorites list, but with the sheer amount of time I have put in while reading, it will always hold a special place in my heart. With all of that being said, I will be reading the next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2149535.Blood_Noir__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter__16_" title="Blood Noir (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter #16) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Noir</a>.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_706302496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/706302496" />
    <a title="T.L." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3291371-t-l"><img alt="T.L." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442954260p2/3291371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/706302496?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.L." class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.L." href="/user/show/3291371-t-l">T.L.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780515144611" href="/book/show/2337583.The_Harlequin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer706302496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14727172672692592906">As much as I bitch about this series, there must be something worthwhile about it, or I'd stop reading it, right?<br/>My complaint with <i>The Harlequin</i> like with the last several books in the series, is, LKH coms up with good titles, and good premises, sets them up and gets you interested then bogs the plot down with one of three things: Too much sex, the Recurring Butt Hurt of Richard, or the Anger is My Name of Dolph the detective. I know with an ongoing series an author has repeating characters and </span>
  <span id="freeText14727172672692592906" style="display:none">As much as I bitch about this series, there must be something worthwhile about it, or I'd stop reading it, right?<br />My complaint with <i>The Harlequin</i> like with the last several books in the series, is, LKH coms up with good titles, and good premises, sets them up and gets you interested then bogs the plot down with one of three things: Too much sex, the Recurring Butt Hurt of Richard, or the Anger is My Name of Dolph the detective. I know with an ongoing series an author has repeating characters and sometimes interactions between those characters and others must be explained in a book in order to set the stage for what's going to happen. I've seen it done in other series...and done <i>better</i>. I don't know if I should bitch slap LKH for being a lazy writer, not creative enough to handle explanations better, or her editor for not correcting LKH.<br />At least with this book we got to chapter 9 before the sexcapades started. I liked the premise of the book, but as usual, it gets lost in all the sex, and tied up all too quickly in a show down that seems rushed. I've been told if I stick out the series at least through <i>Bullet</i>, my patience will be rewarded. We'll see.<br />I'm off to start <i>Blood Noir</i>. Cross your fingers for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14727172672692592906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x+M1080dCu9Xk9deLYHKZqewHqrcbKKI3mgtlHDNT2R+TX1ekB807jv9+NYQ0vFquYaVN34dkfuuXXkz8QndJA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  <span id="freeText1230963409387135149" style="display:none">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis with her family.</span>
